# Java Service Initialization Lifecycle Pattern in Kafka

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the Startable/Stoppable service lifecycle: the Lifecycle interface (or equivalent), the service startup ordering, and the coordinated shutdown sequence that ensures dependent services stop in reverse order.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

  1003→    /**
  1004→     * Closes all the provided closeables.
  1005→     * @throws IOException if any of the close methods throws an IOException.
  1006→     *         The first IOException is thrown with subsequent exceptions
  1007→     *         added as suppressed exceptions.
  1008→     */
  1009→    public static void closeAll(Closeable... closeables) throws IOException {
  1010→        IOException exception = null;
  1011→        for (Closeable closeable : closeables) {
  1012→            try {
  1013→                if (closeable != null)
  1014→                    closeable.close();
  1015→            } catch (IOException e) {
  1016→                if (exception != null)
  1017→                    exception.addSuppressed(e);
  1018→                else
  1019→                    exception = e;
  1020→            }
  1021→        }
  1022→        if (exception != null)
  1023→            throw exception;
  1024→    }

   729→  override def shutdown(timeout: Duration): Unit = {
   730→    if (!maybeChangeStatus(STARTED, SHUTTING_DOWN)) return
   731→    try {
   732→      val deadline = time.milliseconds() + timeout.toMillis
   733→      info("shutting down")
   734→
   735→      if (config.controlledShutdownEnable) {
   736→        if (replicaManager != null)
   737→          replicaManager.beginControlledShutdown()
   738→
   739→        if (lifecycleManager != null) {
   740→          lifecycleManager.beginControlledShutdown()
   741→          try {
   742→            val controlledShutdownTimeoutMs = deadline - time.milliseconds()
   743→            lifecycleManager.controlledShutdownFuture.get(controlledShutdownTimeoutMs, TimeUnit.MILLISECONDS)
   744→          } catch {
   745→            case _: TimeoutException =>
   746→              error("Timed out waiting for the controller to approve controlled shutdown")
   747→            case e: Throwable =>
   748→              error("Got unexpected exception waiting for controlled shutdown future", e)
   749→          }
   750→        }
   751→      }
   752→      if (lifecycleManager != null)
   753→        lifecycleManager.beginShutdown()
   754→
   755→      // Stop socket server to stop accepting any more connections and requests.
   756→      // Socket server will be shutdown towards the end of the sequence.
   757→      if (socketServer != null) {
   758→        CoreUtils.swallow(socketServer.stopProcessingRequests(), this)
   759→      }
   760→      metadataPublishers.forEach(p => sharedServer.loader.removeAndClosePublisher(p).get())
   761→      metadataPublishers.clear()
   762→      if (dataPlaneRequestHandlerPool != null)
   763→        CoreUtils.swallow(dataPlaneRequestHa

   109→  private def maybeChangeStatus(from: ProcessStatus, to: ProcessStatus): Boolean = {
   110→    lock.lock()
   111→    try {
   112→      if (status != from) return false
   113→      status = to
   114→      if (to == SHUTDOWN) awaitShutdownCond.signalAll()
   115→    } finally {
   116→      lock.unlock()
   117→    }
   118→    true
   119→  }

   100→  override def shutdown(): Unit = {
   101→    // In combined mode, we want to shut down the broker first, since the controller may be
   102→    // needed for controlled shutdown. Additionally, the controller shutdown process currently
   103→    // stops the raft client early on, which would disrupt broker shutdown.
   104→    broker.foreach(_.shutdown())
   105→    controller.foreach(_.shutdown())
   106→    CoreUtils.swallow(AppInfoParser.unregisterAppInfo(Server.MetricsPrefix, config.brokerId.toString, metrics), this)
   107→  }
   108→
   109→  override def awaitShutdown(): Unit = {
   110→    broker.foreach(_.awaitShutdown())
   111→    controller.foreach(_.awaitShutdown())
   112→  }
   113→}

Based on my thorough analysis of the Kafka repository at `/workspace/kafka--0753c489`, I've identified the core lifecycle interface and implementation patterns used for coordinated startup and shutdown. Here are my findings:

### 1. Core Lifecycle Interface

**File: `/workspace/kafka--0753c489/core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/Server.scala`**

```scala
trait Server {
  def startup(): Unit
  def shutdown(): Unit
  def awaitShutdown(): Unit
}
```

This is the foundational lifecycle trait that all major server components implement. It defines three key methods:
- `startup()`: Initialize and start the service
- `shutdown()`: Gracefully shut down the service
- `awaitShutdown()`: Block until shutdown is complete

The same file defines state transitions:

```scala
sealed trait ProcessStatus
```

/**
 * The broker lifecycle manager owns the broker state.
 *
 * Its inputs are messages passed in from other parts of the broker and from the
 * controller: requests to start up, or shut down, for example. Its output are the broker
 * state and various futures that can be used to wait for broker state transitions to
 * occur.
 *
 * The lifecycle manager handles registering the broker with the controller, as described
 * in KIP-631. After registration is complete, it handles sending periodic broker
 * heartbeats and processing the responses.
 *
 * This code uses an event queue paradigm. Modifications get translated into events, which
 * are placed on the queue to be processed sequentially. As described in the JavaDoc for
 * each variable, most mutable state can be accessed only from that event queue thread.
 * In some cases we expose a volatile variable which can be read from any thread, but only
 * written from the event queue thread.
 */

    builder.append(" id=").append(config.nodeId)
    builder.append("] ")
    builder.toString()
  }

  this.logIdent = logContext.logPrefix()

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Kafka service lifecycle pattern. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed findings about Apache Kafka's Startable/Stoppable service lifecycle implementation. The analysis includes:

### Core Findings:

1. **Lifecycle Interface**: The `Server` trait in `kafka/server/Server.scala` defines the core lifecycle contract with `startup()`, `shutdown()`, and `awaitShutdown()` methods.

2. **Top-Level Orchestration**: `KafkaRaftServer` coordinates both broker and controller startup in dependency order (controller first, broker second).

3. **LIFO Shutdown Sequence**: `BrokerServer` and `ControllerServer` implement reverse-order shutdown:
   - Services that depend on the scheduler are stopped before the scheduler itself
   - All request handling halts before closing network layers
   - Storage and persistence happens before final shutdown

4. **Coordinator Services**: `GroupCoordinatorService` and `ShareCoordinatorService` implement Java-based lifecycle with atomic state management.

5. **Utility Methods**: `Utils.java` provides critical shutdown orchestration:
   - `closeAll()`: Aggregates exceptions from multiple closeable resources
   - `closeAllQuietly()`: Graceful closure with error tracking
   - `tryAll()`: Executes all functions even if exceptions occur

6. **Cascading Dependencies**: Components like `ReplicaManager` shut down all dependent services in proper order (fetchers, purgatories, plugins).

The answer JSON includes 18 relevant source files, key symbols, the shutdown chain, and a detailed narrative explaining how the coordinated lifecycle pattern ensures proper resource cleanup and prevents conflicts through dependency-aware ordering.

BrokerServer Implementation\n\n**File: `/workspace/kafka--0753c489/core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerServer.scala`**\n\nThis class manages all broker-level services and implements careful shutdown ordering:\n\n**Shutdown sequence (lines 729-843):**\n\n1. **Controlled shutdown phase**: Notify controller and wait for approval\n2. **Request processing**: Stop accepting new requests\n3. **Request handlers**: Shutdown the pool of request processors\n4. **API processors**: Close KafkaApis\n5. **Scheduler**: Critical early shutdown to prevent interference with other services\n6. **Coordinators**: Shutdown transaction and group coordinators\n7. **Replica Manager**: Shutdown replica fetcher threads and purgatory\n8. **Alter Partition Manager**: Handle pending partition state changes\n9. **Channel managers**: Close communication channels\n10. **Log Manager**: Persist state before closing\n11. **Remote log manager**: Close gracefully\n12. **Quota managers**: Shutdown quota enforcement\n13. **Socket server**: Final shutdown of network layer\n14. **Lifecycle manager**: Signal broker is down\n\n**Key code snippet showing sequential shutdown:**\n```scala\noverride def shutdown(timeout: Duration): Unit = {\n  if (!maybeChangeStatus(STARTED, SHUTTING_DOWN)) return\n  try {\n    // ... controlled shutdown logic ...\n    if (socketServer != null) {\n      CoreUtils.swallow(socketServer.stopProcessingRequests(), this)\n    }\n    // ... handler pool shutdown ...\n    // Critical early scheduler shutdown\n    if (kafkaScheduler != null)\n      CoreUtils.swallow(kafkaScheduler.shutdown(), this)\n    \n    // Coordinators\n    if (transactionCoordinator != null)\n      CoreUtils.swallow(transactionCoordinator.shutdown(), this)\n    if (groupCoordinator != null)\n      CoreUtils.swallow(groupCoordinator.shutdown(), this)\n    \n    // Core services\n    if (replicaManager != null)\n      CoreUtils.swallow(replicaManager.shutdown(), this)\n    if (logManager != null)\n      CoreUtils.swallow(logManager.shutdown(brokerEpoch), this)\n    // ... etc ...\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### 5. ControllerServer Implementation\n\n**File: `/workspace/kafka--0753c489/core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ControllerServer.scala`**\n\nSimilar structured shutdown (lines 433-485):\n\n```scala\ndef shutdown(): Unit = {\n  if (!maybeChangeStatus(STARTED, SHUTTING_DOWN)) return\n  try {\n    info(\"shutting down\")\n    // Ensure not raft leader\n    sharedServer.ensureNotRaftLeader()\n    \n    // Metadata publishers\n    metadataPublishers.forEach(p => sharedServer.loader.removeAndClosePublisher(p).get())\n    metadataPublishers.clear()\n    \n    // Socket server\n    if (socketServer != null)\n      CoreUtils.swallow(socketServer.stopProcessingRequests(), this)\n    \n    // Controller runtime\n    if (controller != null)\n      controller.beginShutdown()\n    \n    if (socketServer != null)\n      CoreUtils.swallow(socketServer.shutdown(), this)\n    \n    // Handler pools and APIs\n    if (controllerApisHandlerPool != null)\n      CoreUtils.swallow(controllerApisHandlerPool.shutdown(), this)\n    \n    // Quotas and cleanup\n    if (quotaManagers != null)\n      CoreUtils.swallow(quotaManagers.shutdown(), this)\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### 6. Shared Infrastructure Layer\n\n**File: `/workspace/kafka--0753c489/core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/SharedServer.scala`**\n\nThe `SharedServer` manages components shared between broker and controller:\n- Raft manager\n- Snapshot generator  \n- Metadata loader\n- Metrics\n\nUses reference-counted semantics:\n```scala\ndef startForBroker(): Unit = synchronized {\n  if (!isUsed()) {\n    start(Endpoints.empty())\n  }\n  usedByBroker = true\n}\n\ndef stopForBroker(): Unit = synchronized {\n  usedByBroker = false\n  if (!isUsed()) {\n    stop()\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### 7. The core architecture is as follows:\\n\\n## Core Lifecycle Interface\\n\\nThe `Server` trait defined in `core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/Server.scala` is the primary lifecycle interface, defining three core methods: `startup()`, `shutdown()`, and `awaitShutdown()`. Its startup follows a dependency-aware order:\\n1. Controller starts first (via `controller.foreach(_.startup())`)\\n2. Broker starts second (via `broker.foreach(_.startup())`)\\n\\nThis ordering ensures that the broker can depend on controller availability for registration and coordination.\\n\\n## BrokerServer Shutdown Pattern\\n\\n**BrokerServer** (`core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerServer.scala`) implements a carefully orchestrated LIFO (Last In, First Out) shutdown sequence that ensures dependent services stop in reverse order. The shutdown orchestration (lines 729-843) follows this sequence:\\n\\n1. Controlled shutdown notification to controller\\n2. Socket server request processing halt\\n3. Request processor pool shutdown\\n4. KafkaApis handler closure\\n5. Scheduler shutdown (critical early shutdown)\\n6. Transaction and group coordinator shutdown\\n7. Replica Manager shutdown (with replica fetcher threads and purgatory)\\n8. Alter Partition Manager shutdown\\n9. Channel managers closure\\n10. Log Manager shutdown with state persistence\\n11. Remote log manager graceful closure\\n12. Quota managers shutdown\\n13. Socket server final shutdown\\n14. Lifecycle manager signal\\n\\nThis sequence ensures that services dependent on scheduler functionality are shut down before the scheduler, and all request handling is halted before closing underlying network and storage components.\\n\\n## ControllerServer Shutdown Pattern\\n\\n**ControllerServer** (`core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ControllerServer.scala`) follows a similar pattern:\\n1. Raft leadership release\\n2. Metadata publishers removal and closure\\n3. Socket server request processing halt\\n4. Controller runtime begin shutdown\\n5. Socket server final shutdown\\n6. API handler pool shutdown\\n7. Quota managers shutdown\\n\\n## Coordinator Services\\n\\n**GroupCoordinatorService** (`group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinatorService.java`) and **ShareCoordinatorService** (`share-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/share/ShareCoordinatorService.java`) implement Java-based lifecycle with atomic state management using `compareAndSet()` for thread-safe status transitions. Both services manage their runtime and metrics through coordinated shutdown using utility methods.\\n\\n## Supporting Lifecycle Components\\n\\n**ReplicaManager** (`core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaManager.scala`) demonstrates cascading shutdown of dependent services:\\n- Log dir failure handlers\\n- Replica fetcher managers (both standard and alter-log-dirs)\\n- Delayed operation purgatories (for fetch, produce, remote operations)\\n- Replica selector plugins\\n\\n**AbstractFetcherManager**, **ReplicaFetcherManager**, **ReplicaAlterLogDirsManager** implement shutdown methods for coordinated termination of replica fetching threads.\\n\\n## Coordinated Shutdown Utilities\\n\\n**Utils.java** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/utils/Utils.java`) provides critical utilities for coordinated shutdown:\\n- `closeAll(Closeable...)`: Closes all closeables with suppressed exception aggregation\\n- `closeAllQuietly(AtomicReference, String, AutoCloseable...)`: Graceful closure with error tracking\\n- `tryAll(List<Callable<Void>>)`: Executes all functions even if exceptions occur, collecting and rethrowing with suppressed exceptions\\n- `closeQuietly(AutoCloseable, String)`: Logs closure failures at WARN level\\n\\n## Dependency Management\\n\\n**SharedServer** (`core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/SharedServer.scala`) manages components shared between broker and controller using reference-counted semantics:\\n- Raft manager\\n- Snapshot generator\\n- Metadata loader\\n- Metrics\\n\\nThis enables either component to start or stop independently while shared resources are properly managed.\\n\\n## State Machine Pattern\\n\\nServices use atomic state transitions through `compareAndSet()` operations to manage state changes: SHUTDOWN \u2192 STARTING \u2192 STARTED \u2192 SHUTTING_DOWN, preventing concurrent startup/shutdown and ensuring idempotent operations.\\n\\nThe overall pattern ensures graceful service termination with proper dependency ordering, preventing resource leaks and ensuring all cleanup operations complete even when individual components fail.\"\n}\n",
